   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">
    List of NCAA Division I institutions
   </h1>
   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
    <div id="siteSub">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div>
    <div id="contentSub">
    </div>
    <div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
     Jump to:
     <a href="#mw-head">
      navigation
     </a>
     ,
     <a href="#p-search">
      search
     </a>
    </div>
    <div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en">
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NCAA_Hall_of_Champions.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/NCAA_Hall_of_Champions.JPG/220px-NCAA_Hall_of_Champions.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/NCAA_Hall_of_Champions.JPG/330px-NCAA_Hall_of_Champions.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/NCAA_Hall_of_Champions.JPG/440px-NCAA_Hall_of_Champions.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NCAA_Hall_of_Champions.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        NCAA Hall of Champions building located in
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indianapolis,_Indiana" title="Indianapolis, Indiana">
         Indianapolis, Indiana
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In the 2013-14 school year, there are 351 American colleges and universities classified as
      <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I" title="NCAA Division I">
       Division I
      </a>
      for
      <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">
       National Collegiate Athletic Association
      </a>
      (NCAA) competition. 49 of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states" title="List of U.S. states">
       50 states
      </a>
      (all except
      <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">
       Alaska
      </a>
      ) are represented. Schools that are in transition to or from Division I are listed below the main listing. This list does not include affiliate members who may play Division I in only one or two sports.
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="In_transition">
       In transition
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_NCAA_Division_I_institutions&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: In transition">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      These schools are in transition to Division I. They are considered by the NCAA to be Division I schools, but they are full members only for scheduling purposes.
     </p>

     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">
       Notes
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_NCAA_Division_I_institutions&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Notes">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="reflist columns references-column-count references-column-count-2" style="-moz-column-count: 2; -webkit-column-count: 2; column-count: 2; list-style-type: decimal;">
      <ol class="references">
       <li id="cite_note-2">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-2">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         The formal nickname for women's teams is "Razorbacks", and the university consistently refers to the women's teams as the Razorbacks or Razorback women. The terms "Lady Razorbacks" and "Lady'Backs" have been abandoned by the university.
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-3">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-3">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         The Long Beach State baseball team is unofficially called "Dirtbags", and the school recognizes the nickname.
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-4">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-4">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         The school is increasingly branding its athletic program as simply "Charleston". The NCAA and national sports media are inconsistent, using "Charleston" for basketball but "College of Charleston" for other sports.
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-5">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-5">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Charleston Southern's women's golf team is known as the Lady Bucs
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-6">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-6">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         The women's basketball team is now the only EKU team using "Lady Colonels". All other women's teams use "Colonels".
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-7">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-7">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         The women's gymnastics team is known as "Gym Dogs".
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-8">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-8">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Most of the university is in Cambridge, but some academic buildings and athletic facilities, including
         <a href="/wiki/Harvard_Stadium" title="Harvard Stadium">
          the football stadium
         </a>
         , lie in Boston.
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-9">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-9">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         In July 2013, all Hawaii men's teams adopted the nickname of "Rainbow Warriors". This reversed a 2000 policy that resulted in different men's teams using "Rainbow Warriors", "Warriors", and "Rainbows". All women's teams continue to use "Rainbow Wahine".
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-10">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-10">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Although UIC is the school's preferred athletic name, national sports media generally use "Illinois-Chicago" in score listings and on first reference.
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-11">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-11">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         National sports media generally use "Loyola-Chicago", "Loyola (Chicago)", or "Loyola (Illinois)" to distinguish this school from others with the Loyola name.
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-12">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-12">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         While national media generally use "Massachusetts", the shortened "UMass" is in wide usage, especially in Massachusetts itself.
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-13">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-13">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         National media sometimes use "Miami (Florida)" or "Miami (FL)" to distinguish it from Miami University in Ohio.
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-14">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-14">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         National media usually use "Miami (Ohio)" or "Miami (OH)" to distinguish it from the University of Miami in Florida.
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-15">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-15">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         National media generally use "Mississippi" in score listings and on first reference, but will frequently use "Ole Miss" on later reference. The school athletic department prefers "Ole Miss".
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-16">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-16">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         The women's basketball team is known as the "
         <a href="/wiki/Montana_Lady_Griz_basketball" title="Montana Lady Griz basketball">
          Lady Griz
         </a>
         ", but all other women's teams use the "Grizzlies" nickname.
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-17">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-17">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         The baseball team is nicknamed "Thoroughbreds" instead of "Racers".
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-18">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-18">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         The school has rebranded its athletic program as "Omaha". its all-sports league, The Summit League, has followed this usage since UNO became a member in 2012. UNO's ice hockey league, the
         <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Hockey_Conference" title="National Collegiate Hockey Conference">
          National Collegiate Hockey Conference
         </a>
         , used "Nebraska-Omaha" in the league's inaugural season in 201314, but now uses "Omaha". National media still use "Nebraska-Omaha".
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-19">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-19">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         The men's basketball team is nicknamed "Runnin' Rebels", while all other teams are known as "Rebels".
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-21">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-21">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         As of November 9, 2011, North Dakota has no athletic nickname. On that day, the state's governor
         <a href="/wiki/Jack_Dalrymple" title="Jack Dalrymple">
          Jack Dalrymple
         </a>
         signed a bill into law that allowed the school to drop its former nickname of Fighting Sioux, ending a long-standing controversy over its use. Under the law, UND cannot adopt a new nickname until January 2015.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
          <a href="#cite_note-20">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           2
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-22">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-22">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         The Penn State women's basketball team is nicknamed "
         <a href="/wiki/Penn_State_Lady_Lions_basketball" title="Penn State Lady Lions basketball">
          Lady Lions
         </a>
         ", but all other women's teams use "Nittany Lions".
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-23">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-23">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         The school also widely uses its historic short form of "Pitt".
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-24">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-24">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         In 2013, the school changed its athletic brand to "St. Francis Brooklyn" in an attempt to distinguish itself from other schools of that name, notably the fellow Northeast Conference member in Pennsylvania. National media usually use "St. Francis (New York)" instead.
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-25">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-25">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         National media usually use "St. Francis (Pennsylvania)" to distinguish it from other schools of that name, notably the fellow Northeast Conference school of the same name in Brooklyn.
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-26">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-26">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Other schools in the U.S. have this name, but national media do not add a location identifier to it, since it is the only "St. John's" whose athletic teams compete in NCAA Division I.
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-27">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-27">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Although there are other schools with this name in the U.S., none of the others are members of Division I. Therefore, national media refer to it as "Saint Joseph's" (preferred usage) or "St. Joseph's", without a regional identifier, or just St. Joe's/Saint Joe's.
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-28">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-28">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Although the school prefers to use "USC Upstate", national media often use "South Carolina Upstate".
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-29">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-29">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         The school accepts either "Southern California" or "USC" for athletics purposes; national news media generally use "USC".
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-30">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-30">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Historically, USC women's teams were known as the "Women of Troy". The school now accepts either "Trojans" or "Women of Troy" for use with women's teams.
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-31">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-31">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Although the school prefers to use "SIUE", national media usually use "SIU Edwardsvile".
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-32">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-32">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         The formal nickname for women's teams is "Lady Volunteers". However, the school considers the use of "Lady Vols" acceptable, and the shortened form is widely popular in Tennessee and in much wider usage among national media than the longer form. Effective with the 201516 school year, almost all women's teams will drop "Lady" from their nicknames, with only women's basketball retaining the
         <a href="/wiki/Tennessee_Lady_Volunteers_basketball" title="Tennessee Lady Volunteers basketball">
          Lady Volunteers
         </a>
         nickname.
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-33">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-33">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         TexasPan American merged with the
         <a href="/wiki/University_of_Texas_at_Brownsville" title="University of Texas at Brownsville">
          University of Texas at Brownsville
         </a>
         in July 2015 to create the new
         <a href="/wiki/University_of_Texas_Rio_Grande_Valley" title="University of Texas Rio Grande Valley">
          University of Texas Rio Grande Valley
         </a>
         (UTRGV). The
         <a href="/wiki/University_of_Texas_System" title="University of Texas System">
          University of Texas System
         </a>
         has confirmed that UTRGV will inherit the UTPA athletic program. The new nickname of
         <a href="/wiki/UTRGV_Vaqueros" title="UTRGV Vaqueros">
          Vaqueros
         </a>
         was announced in November 2014. Although the choice came under fire from several quarters, in February 2015 the school unveiled the new Vacqueros graphics and plans for implementing the changes before the start of the 2015-16 school year.
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-34">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-34">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         The women's basketball team is known as "
         <a href="/wiki/Texas_Tech_Lady_Raiders_basketball" title="Texas Tech Lady Raiders basketball">
          Lady Raiders
         </a>
         ". All other women's teams use "Red Raiders".
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-35">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-35">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         The men's basketball team is nicknamed "Runnin' Utes", and the women's gymnastics team is nicknamed "Red Rocks".
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-36">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-36">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         The school's formal name is Virginia Polytechnic Institute and State University, but it uses "Virginia Tech" in all but the most formal contexts.
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-37">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-37">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         The school prefers "Green Bay" for its athletic program, and accepts "GB". National sports media were slow to adopt this, generally using "Wisconsin-Green Bay", but the school's preferred usage has become generally accepted since 2011.
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-38">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-38">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         The school officially uses "Milwaukee" for its athletic program, and accepts "UWM". As with Green Bay, national media were slow to accept this, preferring "WisconsinMilwaukee", but "Milwaukee" is now seeing wide media use.
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-Southland_2013-39">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         ^
         <a href="#cite_ref-Southland_2013_39-0">
          <sup>
           <i>
            <b>
             a
            </b>
           </i>
          </sup>
         </a>
         <a href="#cite_ref-Southland_2013_39-1">
          <sup>
           <i>
            <b>
             b
            </b>
           </i>
          </sup>
         </a>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Joined the
         <a href="/wiki/Southland_Conference" title="Southland Conference">
          Southland Conference
         </a>
         in July, 2013.
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-WAC_2013-41">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-WAC_2013_41-0">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Joined the
         <a href="/wiki/Western_Athletic_Conference" title="Western Athletic Conference">
          WAC
         </a>
         in July, 2013.
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-America_East_2013-44">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-America_East_2013_44-0">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Joined the
         <a href="/wiki/America_East_Conference" title="America East Conference">
          America East Conference
         </a>
         in July 2013.
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-47">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-47">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Began transitioning to Division I in July 2012 as member of Atlantic Sun Conference; full membership in July 2016; switched to Horizon League on July 1, 2015
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NKU_46-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-NKU-46">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           7
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
        </span>
       </li>
      </ol>
     </div>
